B0041B785Y|3|I guess I'll have to apologize in advance for not thinking that every album by my favorite Metal band of the last twelve years is perfect.  I was relatively late to the Meshuggah party, as Chaosphere was when I jumped on the train, and, to date, is still my favorite release (by the smallest of margins).  While DEI is an unbelievable record which possesses one of Metal's greatest tracks, Future Breed Machine, Chaosphere, in my opinion, was simply more consistent from start to finish.<br /><br />To give an idea of where my review is coming from, I should state that Nothing, while totally original in terms of direction, is my least favorite record from these guys.  The first twelve minutes of \\"I\\" is near-perfection.  While Catch 33 is a bold record that shows their songwriting ambition (the ethereal guitar sections are its best feature), it contains too much of Nothing's style of one-note riffing for my taste.  Obzen, in my opinion, was a fantastic amalgam of their post-DEI style.  I'm a huge fan of old-school Thrash, and Combustion was *exactly* the track I was waiting for Meshuggah to make; it's literally Thrash-done-Meshuggah-style.  In fact, I think Combustion ranks right up there with Future Breed Machine.  While the one-note riffs are still there, they incorporated more of Chaosphere's staccato muting, and, for me, the direction was perfect.<br /><br />That brings me to Koloss.  After about a dozen full listens, I think I have developed a sufficient enough opinion.  My expectations were *not* for the record to sound like another record; I just wanted to love it for whatever it is.  Unfortunately, I just *like* it.  It's pointless to mention production value, as Meshuggah know what it takes to make their records sound great, and it sounds as good as ever, here.<br /><br />\\"I Am Colossus\\" is a solid opener, and contains very straight-forward riffing (relative to Meshuggah).  I'm a sucker for triplet-based tracks with this feel, and this one doesn't disappoint.  Tomas was correct when he said that the two notes Frederik plays during the solo are all that was necessary to make it sound great.  The supporting rhythm riff during the solo is, to me, the standout section of this track.<br /><br />\\"The Demons Name Is Surveillance\\" is one of two fast/more driving tracks on the record, and, while its 6/8-double-bass feel is wonderfully played (does anyone really need to continue emphasizing how tight these guys are?), the notes/riffs just don't grab me.  The higher-note bends that are done during what might be called the second Meshuggah-chorus (which is never truly a chorus ;) just seem a bit gratuitous.  The solo isn't particularly noteworthy (no pun intended), as it's Thordendal's typical tapping, and it doesn't sound very inspired.  It sounds as if this track was trying to be the Koloss version of Bleed.  The endings are similar, but the exclamation point put on the end of Bleed is not even close to being matched, here.<br /><br />\\"Do Not Look Down\\" is what I believe a Nothing track *should* have sounded more like.  As a drummer, I love the fact that Haake's pocket is so deep.  Meshuggah isn't what I would call a \\"groove\\" band per se, but the fact that they have such a great pocket makes their brand of Metal that much more enjoyable.  The riffs themselves during this track just have a much freer/less-intentional feel to them, and the solo is one of the best that Thordendal's done in a while.  I love the effect that was added to the last few notes of it!  He took a break from the tapping and let all of us know, once again, that he can own with the traditional picking style.<br /><br />\\"Behind the Sun\\" doesn't grab me, at all.  While Meshuggah are quite capable of producing slow/brooding tunes that are effective, I don't feel that this is one of them.  It's usually a difficult task to make this type tune hold interest, and this one just doesn't quite do it.  I find myself listening *only* because it's Meshuggah playing it, and simply hearing well-played music is sometimes enough for me.  The second half of the tune is serviceable, but that's about it.<br /><br />\\"The Hurt That Finds You First\\", the first two-thirds of which is quite Thrashy, just didn't quite hit the mark until, strangely for me, the speed was over.  I quite enjoy the ambient/relaxed material these guys do, and the outro is nicely done.  Like TDNIS, I just didn't like the notes that they chose to go with the respective feels, and I really do believe that they could have done better.  Take a listen to \\"Terminal Illusions\\" or \\"Combustion\\", and you'll hear Thrash riffs that mean far more than anything played, here.  To me, this tune would be a really good Thrash tune for any other band, but, for Meshuggah, it's merely decent.<br /><br />\\"Marrow\\" is nothing more than a b-side/cutting-floor track from Nothing.  While my opinion may seem slanted because of the song's Nothing influence, I really don't think it would have even stood out if it were *on* Nothing. The only reason to listen the tune is because of Haake's excellent performance.<br /><br />\\"Break Those Bones Whose Sinews Gave It Motion\\" is one of two tunes that's grown on me since I starting listening to it.  This is slowness-done-right.  In context, the riffs really do work well with each other, and the parts never seem gratuitous.  This is a standout track on the record.<br /><br />\\"Swarm\\" is a track that, while solid and consistent with a good feel that they haven't done in years, just never quite takes off as anything special.  There are no riffs that really stand out.  This is yet another missed opportunity, and the ending is just plain lazy.<br /><br />\\"Demiurge\\" is the other tune that has started to grow on me.  In terms of feel, Meshuggah really hasn't ever done a track like this one, and that's why I really didn't know what to think, at first.  It's hard to describe the feel of what might be called Meshuggah-verses here, but it's almost a....rebellious feel?  I know that there's a better word for it, but I'm currently at a loss.  It sort of reminds me of the approach of \\"Up Lift\\" from Reinventing the Steel.  That said, while the majority of the tune is quite good, this is another case where I believe the outro should have been a little less lazy.<br /><br />\\"The Last Vigil\\" is a nice outro that fits quite well with the scheme of the record.  As has been pointed out, it has that Catch 33 feel to it, and the fact that Koloss ends this way isn't at all a detriment.<br /><br />My Standout Tracks:<br />I Am Colossus<br />Do Not Look Down<br />Break Those Bones Whose Sinews Gave it Motion<br />Demiurge<br /><br />I'm sorry for the levity, and I apologize if none of this was helpful/interesting.  I started typing and couldn't stop!  Meshuggah is one of the only bands that brings it out!<br /><br />Meshuggah have the luxury in that they have to *try* to make a bad album.  That hasn't happened here, but it could have been so much more.

B00AEBBA36|5|Exceptional. Very realistic.    Be advised: Lots of killing in a film about a real battle where many brave men - on both sides - were killed. Grueling and hard to watch at times, due to the sheer gruesomeness of the battle scenes.    This movie truly seems to capture the horror and utter chaos of this historic battle of the Viet Nam war. There is actually real film available from this battle, as well as the best-selling book, not to mention those brave men who were there and lived to tell about it. This film seems to be a reasonably faithful version of what really happened - at least from the American standpoint.    So, if you think this is just a valentine to the American military with little basis in fact, you are mistaken, as the VC are portrayed as courageous and competent fighters. Truth is stranger than fiction, and no make-believe Hollywood story has anything on We Were Soldiers. This fight really took place, with both sides taking extremely heavy losses.    Yes, it is quite gory, but certainly no less so than the actual battle must have been. With so many bullets and bombs flying around in such close quarters, it had to have been hell on earth.    These men were astoundingly brave and their story deserves to be told. Such amazing courage needs to be remembered, and such profound sacrifice should not be sugarcoated.    I honestly cannot fathom why any viewer would give this film less than three stars. Perhaps some people are just so opposed to violence in general, or the Viet Nam war in particular, that they dislike any film portraying our military in an even a vaguely honorable light. I personally feel the war was a waste, yet I still think the world of those men and women who were brave enough to go and fight it, not because they wanted to, but because they had to. To any and all remaining survivors of this battle, you have my utmost admiration.    A truly emotional film. A real story that every American interested in history should be made aware of.

Having dug into several dozen, I can say that not one of them is perfect, each lacking something here or there, some feature(s) that another one has, isn't as easy to use, etc.  Though I keep two different editors installed, my default goto editor has been [[ASIN:B004OZK9VW PicSay Pro]], which is what I'll be using as a comparison in this review.  In terms of cost, PicShop and PicSay Pro are pretty close, with just a dollar separating them.  Both have free trial versions, so you can have a chance to check them out before plopping down your cash.<br /><br />As expected, I found a lot of things with PicShop that weren't up to the caliber of PicSay Pro, and PicSay Pro lacked some of the features of PicShop.  You can share right from your gallery into PicSay Pro, but not PicShop.  Exporting pictures is quite limited with PicShop, with only exporting to your device, Twitter, or Facebook.  PicSay Pro on the other hand can also export to anything you can normally share to on your device, plus set as image for a contact or set as your wallpaper.  PicSay Pro also lets you save the image locally where you want and under any name you want, while PicShop saves in the same location as the original photo under whatever name it chooses.  It's not all bad for PicShop though.  It can save in more formats automatically, upscaling your image on its own when needed.  Resaving an edited image results in a new file with a new name, so the original isn't overwritten.  In PicSay Pro, you have to set the new name manually.  Filters, effects, and additional features again goes it PicSay Pro, which has a much larger set of these.  PicShop fights back though with the ability to layer images, and use frames on your final output.  The UI for both apps is pretty easy to use, though they differ significantly.  PicShop may win this argument by a smidgen, because of it's larger buttons, sliders, and filter previews.<br /><br />So far, not a single issue with performance of PicShop.  It worked well, and at my slightest touch.  Stability has been excellent as well.
